{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"call_b4458a491e16451294098121","type":"tool_result","content":"1\t# gribtract\n2\t\n3\tA pure-Rust GRIB2 decoder — decodes NOAA/WMO GRIB2 messages into typed fields and gridded numeric data, verified field-by-field against eccodes/wgrib2.\n4\t\n5\tNo C dependencies for core GRIB2 decoding (DRT 5.0, 5.2, 5.3, 5.41). No shelling out to `wgrib2`. JPEG2000 (DRT 5.40) requires the optional `jpeg2000` feature, which pulls in `openjpeg-sys` (C FFI).\n6\t\n7\t## What is GRIB2?\n8\t\n9\tGRIB2 (GRIdded Binary, Edition 2) is the binary file format used by NOAA, ECMWF, and other national weather services to distribute model output — temperature, wind, precipitation, pressure fields on global and regional grids. It is the primary output format for GFS, HRRR, NBM, GEFS, NAM, and similar NWP (numerical weather prediction) products.\n10\t\n11\tDecoding GRIB2 requires handling: multi-section message framing, grid geometry definitions (lat/lon, Lambert conformal, polar stereographic, Gaussian), parameter tables indexed by discipline/category/number, five or more data packing algorithms (simple, complex, spatial-differencing, JPEG2000, PNG), and bitmaps for missing-value masking.\n12\t\n13\tThe standard tools (`wgrib2`, `eccodes`) are C programs and libraries. If you need to decode GRIB2 in a Rust project, your options have been to shell out to them, call their C APIs through FFI, or skip decoded values and work with raw bytes.\n14\t\n15\tgribtract is a native Rust alternative.\n16\t\n17\t## Features\n18\t\n19\t- **Pure Rust for core formats** — no C toolchain or FFI for DRT 5.0, 5.2, 5.3, 5.41 (simple, complex, complex+spatial differencing, PNG). JPEG2000 (DRT 5.40) requires the optional `jpeg2000` feature, which uses `openjpeg-sys` (C FFI)\n20\t- **Typed output** — decoded fields carry structured metadata: parameter ID, level, forecast time, grid geometry\n21\t- **Multiple packing formats** — DRT 5.0 (simple), 5.2 (complex), 5.3 (complex+spatial differencing), 5.40 (JPEG2000), 5.41 (PNG)\n22\t- **Multiple grid projections** — lat/lon (GDT 3.0), polar stereographic (3.20), Lambert conformal (3.30), Gaussian (3.40)\n23\t- **Lazy decode path** — parse headers and defer grid data; extract individual grid points in O(1) for DRT=0 fields without full decode\n24\t- **Timeseries extractor** — given a decoded GRIB2 message set, extract per-station forecasts for a list of lat/lon coordinates\n25\t- **Python bindings** — `gribtract-py` (PyO3) exposes the Rust decoder to Python\n26\t- **Oracle-gated correctness** — every release is verified against eccodes/wgrib2 over a corpus of real NOAA files\n27\t\n28\t## Crate Layout\n29\t\n30\t```\n31\tgribtract/\n32\t├── crates/\n33\t│   ├── gribtract-core     # Section parser, template decoders, unpacking. No I/O.\n34\t│   ├── gribtract          # High-level API: message iterator, field selection, timeseries\n35\t│   ├── gribtract-cli      # `gribtract decode|list|dump` command-line tool\n36\t│   ├── gribtract-py       # Python bindings via PyO3 (excluded from default build)\n37\t│   └── gribtract-testutil # Differential harness utilities: corpus, golden, diff\n38\t└── xtask                  # Corpus management, reference-decoder runner, bench dashboard\n39\t```\n40\t\n41\t`gribtract-core` is the zero-dependency parsing core. `gribtract` is the crate you depend on for library use. `gribtract-cli` provides a standalone binary.\n42\t\n43\t## Usage\n44\t\n45\tAdd to `Cargo.toml`:\n46\t\n47\t```toml\n48\t[dependencies]\n49\tgribtract = \"0.1\"\n50\t```\n51\t\n52\t### Decode all fields from a GRIB2 file\n53\t\n54\t```rust\n55\tuse gribtract::{decode, Field};\n56\t\n57\tlet bytes = std::fs::read(\"hrrr.t00z.wrfsfcf01.grib2\")?;\n58\tlet fields: Vec<Field> = gribtract::decode(&bytes)?;\n59\t\n60\tfor field in &fields {\n61\t    println!(\n62\t        \"param={}/{}/{}  level={}  forecast_offset={}h\",\n63\t        field.parameter.discipline,\n64\t        field.parameter.category,\n65\t        field.parameter.number,\n66\t        field.level.value1(),\n67\t        field.forecast_time.offset_seconds() / 3600,\n68\t    );\n69\t}\n70\t```\n71\t\n72\t### Extract a single grid point (DRT=0, O(1))\n73\t\n74\t```rust\n75\tuse gribtract::{decode_lazy, decode_point_drt0};\n76\t\n77\tlet fields = gribtract::decode_lazy(&bytes)?;\n78\tfor lf in &fields {\n79\t    if let Some(body) = &lf.section7_raw {\n80\t        // idx is the flat grid index for your target lat/lon\n81\t        let idx = lf.grid.nearest_index(40.64, -73.78)?;\n82\t        if let Some(value) = decode_point_drt0(body, &lf.packing, idx) {\n83\t            println!(\"value at JFK: {}\", value);\n84\t        }\n85\t    }\n86\t}\n87\t```\n88\t\n89\t### Extract a forecast timeseries  stations: vec![\n99\t        Station { id: \"JFK\".into(),  lat: 40.64,  lon: -73.78  },\n100\t        Station { id: \"ORD\".into(),  lat: 41.979, lon: -87.905 },\n101\t        Station { id:  }\n113\t}\n114\t```\n115\t\n116\t### Decode a DRT=3 (complex+spatial differencing) grid — extract many stations\n117\t\n118\tDRT=3 requires a full sequential decode; random access is not possible. The recommended pattern is decode-once-extract-many:\n119\t\n120\t```rust\n121\tuse gribtract::{decode_lazy, decode_all_drt3};\n122\t\n123\tlet lazy_fields = gribtract::decode_lazy(&bytes)?;\n124\tfor lf in &lazy_fields {\n125\t    if let (Some(body), Some(extra)) = (&lf.section7_raw, &lf.complex_extra) {\n126\t        let n = lf.grid.num_data_points as usize;\n127\t        let grid: Vec<f64> = decode_all_drt3(body, &lf.packing, extra, n)?;\n128\t\n129\t        // Now extract any number of stations by index in O(1) each\n130\t        for (lat, lon) in &station_coords {\n131\t            let idx = lf.grid.nearest_index(*lat, *lon)?;\n132\t            println!(\"value: {}\", grid[idx]);\n133\t        }\n134\t    }\n135\t}\n136\t```\n137\t\n138\t## The Correctness Oracle\n139\t\n140\tgribtract is built **oracle-first**: correctness is defined as agreement with eccodes/wgrib2, not as passing hand-written unit tests.\n141\t\n142\tThe differential harness in `gribtract-testutil` runs both decoders over a corpus of real NOAA GRIB2 files (GFS, HRRR, NBM, GEFS), then compares:\n143\t\n144\t- **Metadata exactly** — center, parameter ID, level, forecast time, grid geometry\n145\t- **Grid values within derived tolerance** — tolerance is computed from the packing template's own scale factors, not an arbitrary epsilon\n146\t\n147\tAny message where gribtract disagrees with the reference decoder becomes a permanent regression fixture. The agreement percentage can only increase; there is no mechanism to silently remove a covered template.\n148\t\n149\t```\n150\tgribtract decode  ─┐\n151\t                   ├─→ compare field-by-field + grid within tolerance\n152\teccodes/wgrib2    ─┘\n153\t```\n154\t\n155\tRun the harness:\n156\t\n157\t```bash\n158\tcargo test -p gribtract -- differential\n159\t```\n160\t\n161\tFetch and run against the full corpus (requires eccodes installed):\n162\t\n163\t```bash\n164\tcargo xtask corpus fetch\n165\tcargo xtask corpus verify\n166\t```\n167\t\n168\t## Performance Dashboard\n169\t\n170\tA self-contained benchmark dashboard (`dashboard.html`) tracks decode throughput on real NOAA files, fed by `bench-results.json`. Speed numbers are never reported without a corresponding correctness verification run.\n171\t\n172\t```bash\n173\t# Run benchmarks and regenerate bench-results.json\n174\tcargo xtask bench\n175\t\n176\t# Serve the live dashboard with streaming benchmark updates\n177\tcargo xtask serve\n178\t```\n179\t\n180\t## Building\n181\t\n182\tRequires Rust 1.75+.\n183\t\n184\t```bash\n185\tgit clone https://github.com/jedarden/gribtract\n186\tcd gribtract\n187\tcargo build --release\n188\t```\n189\t\n190\tThe `gribtract-py` Python extension is excluded from the default workspace build (it requires Python headers for PyO3). It is a thin wrapper over the library API and is intended for ad-hoc inspection rather than production use.\n211\t\n212\t## License\n213\t\n214\tMIT OR Apache-2.0\n215\t"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"15b7b690-050d-4531-b1dc-7cbac43bf258","uuid":"2ca60b25-e5e1-4892-ac0e-e7181889c08f","timestamp":"2026-07-02T15:30:30.571Z","tool_use_result":{"type":"text","file":{"filePath":"/home/coding/gribtract/README.md","content":"# gribtract\n\nA pure-Rust GRIB2 decoder — decodes NOAA/WMO GRIB2 messages into typed fields and gridded numeric data, verified field-by-field against eccodes/wgrib2.\n\nNo C dependencies for core GRIB2 decoding (DRT 5.0, 5.2, 5.3, 5.41). No shelling out to `wgrib2`. JPEG2000 (DRT 5.40) requires the optional `jpeg2000` feature, which pulls in `openjpeg-sys` (C FFI).\n\n## What is GRIB2?\n\nGRIB2 (GRIdded Binary, Edition 2) is the binary file format used by NOAA, ECMWF, and other national weather services to distribute model output — temperature, wind, precipitation, pressure fields on global and regional grids. It is the primary output format for GFS, HRRR, NBM, GEFS, NAM, and similar NWP (numerical weather prediction) products.\n\nDecoding GRIB2 requires handling: multi-section message framing, grid geometry definitions (lat/lon, Lambert conformal, polar stereographic, Gaussian), parameter tables indexed by discipline/category/number, five or more data packing algorithms (simple, complex, spatial-differencing, JPEG2000, PNG), and bitmaps for missing-value masking.\n\nThe standard tools (`wgrib2`, `eccodes`) are C programs and libraries. If you need to decode GRIB2 in a Rust project, your options have been to shell out to them, call their C APIs through FFI, or skip decoded values and work with raw bytes.\n\ngribtract is a native Rust alternative.\n\n## Features\n\n- **Pure Rust for core formats** — no C toolchain or FFI for DRT 5.0, 5.2, 5.3, 5.41 (simple, complex, complex+spatial differencing, PNG). JPEG2000 (DRT 5.40) requires the optional `jpeg2000` feature, which uses `openjpeg-sys` (C FFI)\n- **Typed output** — decoded fields carry structured metadata: parameter ID, level, forecast time, grid geometry\n- **Multiple packing formats** — DRT 5.0 (simple), 5.2 (complex), 5.3 (complex+spatial differencing), 5.40 (JPEG2000), 5.41 (PNG)\n- **Multiple grid projections** — lat/lon (GDT 3.0), polar stereographic (3.20), Lambert conformal (3.30), Gaussian (3.40)\n- **Lazy decode path** — parse headers and defer grid data; extract individual grid points in O(1) for DRT=0 fields without full decode\n- **Timeseries extractor** — given a decoded GRIB2 message set, extract per-station forecasts for a list of lat/lon coordinates\n- **Python bindings** — `gribtract-py` (PyO3) exposes the Rust decoder to Python\n- **Oracle-gated correctness** — every release is verified against eccodes/wgrib2 over a corpus of real NOAA files\n\n## Crate Layout\n\n```\ngribtract/\n├── crates/\n│   ├── gribtract-core     # Section parser, template decoders, unpacking. No I/O.\n│   ├── gribtract          # High-level API: message iterator, field selection, timeseries\n│   ├── gribtract-cli      # `gribtract decode|list|dump` command-line tool\n│   ├── gribtract-py       # Python bindings via PyO3 (excluded from default build)\n│   └── gribtract-testutil # Differential harness utilities: corpus, golden, diff\n└── xtask                  # Corpus management, reference-decoder runner, bench dashboard\n```\n\n`gribtract-core` is the zero-dependency parsing core. `gribtract` is the crate you depend on for library use. `gribtract-cli` provides a standalone binary.\n\n## Usage\n\nAdd to `Cargo.toml`:\n\n```toml\n[dependencies]\ngribtract = \"0.1\"\n```\n\n### Decode all fields from a GRIB2 file\n\n```rust\nuse gribtract::{decode, Field};\n\nlet bytes = std::fs::read(\"hrrr.t00z.wrfsfcf01.grib2\")?;\nlet fields: Vec<Field> = gribtract::decode(&bytes)?;\n\nfor field in &fields {\n    println!(\n        \"param={}/{}/{}  level={}  forecast_offset={}h\",\n        field.parameter.discipline,\n        field.parameter.category,\n        field.parameter.number,\n        field.level.value1(),\n        field.forecast_time.offset_seconds() / 3600,\n    );\n}\n```\n\n### Extract a single grid point (DRT=0, O(1))\n\n```rust\nuse gribtract::{decode_lazy, decode_point_drt0};\n\nlet fields = gribtract::decode_lazy(&bytes)?;\nfor lf in &fields {\n    if let Some(body) = &lf.section7_raw {\n        // idx is the flat grid index for your target lat/lon\n        let idx = lf.grid.nearest_index(40.64, -73.78)?;\n        if let Some(value) = decode_point_drt0(body, &lf.packing, idx) {\n            println!(\"value at JFK: {}\", value);\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Extract a forecast timeseries for a list of stations\n\n```rust\nuse gribtract::timeseries::{extract_timeseries, ParameterRecord, Station, TimeseriesRequest};\n\n// 2m temperature (discipline=0, category=0, number=0), height-above-ground level (type=103)\nlet request = TimeseriesRequest {\n    parameter: ParameterRecord { discipline: 0, category: 0, number: 0 },\n    level_type1: 103,\n    stations: vec![\n        Station { id: \"JFK\".into(),  lat: 40.64,  lon: -73.78  },\n        Station { id: \"ORD\".into(),  lat: 41.979, lon: -87.905 },\n        Station { id: \"LAX\".into(),  lat: 33.943, lon: -118.408 },\n    ],\n};\n\nlet fields = gribtract::decode(&bytes)?;\nlet ts = extract_timeseries(&fields, &request);\n\nfor (station, rows) in &ts.stations {\n    println!(\"Station: {}\", station);\n    for row in rows {\n        println!(\"  forecast hour {}: {:?}\", row.forecast_hour, row.value);\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Decode a DRT=3 (complex+spatial differencing) grid — extract many stations\n\nDRT=3 requires a full sequential decode; random access is not possible. The recommended pattern is decode-once-extract-many:\n\n```rust\nuse gribtract::{decode_lazy, decode_all_drt3};\n\nlet lazy_fields = gribtract::decode_lazy(&bytes)?;\nfor lf in &lazy_fields {\n    if let (Some(body), Some(extra)) = (&lf.section7_raw, &lf.complex_extra) {\n        let n = lf.grid.num_data_points as usize;\n        let grid: Vec<f64> = decode_all_drt3(body, &lf.packing, extra, n)?;\n\n        // Now extract any number of stations by index in O(1) each\n        for (lat, lon) in &station_coords {\n            let idx = lf.grid.nearest_index(*lat, *lon)?;\n            println!(\"value: {}\", grid[idx]);\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n## The Correctness Oracle\n\ngribtract is built **oracle-first**: correctness is defined as agreement with eccodes/wgrib2, not as passing hand-written unit tests.\n\nThe differential harness in `gribtract-testutil` runs both decoders over a corpus of real NOAA GRIB2 files (GFS, HRRR, NBM, GEFS), then compares:\n\n- **Metadata exactly** — center, parameter ID, level, forecast time, grid geometry\n- **Grid values within derived tolerance** — tolerance is computed from the packing template's own scale factors, not an arbitrary epsilon\n\nAny message where gribtract disagrees with the reference decoder becomes a permanent regression fixture. The agreement percentage can only increase; there is no mechanism to silently remove a covered template.\n\n```\ngribtract decode  ─┐\n                   ├─→ compare field-by-field + grid within tolerance\neccodes/wgrib2    ─┘\n```\n\nRun the harness:\n\n```bash\ncargo test -p gribtract -- differential\n```\n\nFetch and run against the full corpus (requires eccodes installed):\n\n```bash\ncargo xtask corpus fetch\ncargo xtask corpus verify\n```\n\n## Performance Dashboard\n\nA self-contained benchmark dashboard (`dashboard.html`) tracks decode throughput on real NOAA files, fed by `bench-results.json`. Speed numbers are never reported without a corresponding correctness verification run.\n\n```bash\n# Run benchmarks and regenerate bench-results.json\ncargo xtask bench\n\n# Serve the live dashboard with streaming benchmark updates\ncargo xtask serve\n```\n\n## Building\n\nRequires Rust 1.75+.\n\n```bash\ngit clone https://github.com/jedarden/gribtract\ncd gribtract\ncargo build --release\n```\n\nThe `gribtract-py` Python extension is excluded from the default workspace build (it requires Python headers for PyO3). Build it explicitly:\n\n```bash\npip install maturin\nmaturin develop -p gribtract-py\n```\n\n## CLI\n\n```bash\n# List all fields in a GRIB2 file (JSON output)\ngribtract list forecast.grib2\n\n# Decode all fields and print as JSON\ngribtract decode forecast.grib2\n\n# Dump grid values for a specific field index\ngribtract dump forecast.grib2 --field 0 --format csv\n```\n\nThe CLI binary is at `crates/gribtract-cli`. It is a thin wrapper over the library API and is intended for ad-hoc inspection rather than production use.\n\n## License\n\nMIT OR Apache-2.0\n","numLines":215,"startLine":1,"totalLines":215}}}
